    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer11801414234943259293">The first suspenseful thriller in the Midnight series from Wall Street Journal bestselling author Melinda Leigh.<br/><br/>Point, click, die.<br/><br/>When two hikers disappear, their hometown in Maine blames the blinding storms. But the truth is far more sinister. Unaware of the danger, tabloid photographer Jayne Sullivan follows an anonymous tip to find the most reclusive sculptor in the art</span>
  <span id="freeText11801414234943259293" style="display:none">The first suspenseful thriller in the Midnight series from Wall Street Journal bestselling author Melinda Leigh.<br /><br />Point, click, die.<br /><br />When two hikers disappear, their hometown in Maine blames the blinding storms. But the truth is far more sinister. Unaware of the danger, tabloid photographer Jayne Sullivan follows an anonymous tip to find the most reclusive sculptor in the art world. Instead, she finds sexy handyman Reed Kimball—and a small town full of fatal secrets.<br /><br />Five years ago, Reed buried his homicide detective career along with his wife. But when a hiker is found dead, the local police chief asks Reed for help. Why was a Celtic coin found under the body? And where is the second hiker? Avoiding the media, Reed doesn’t need a murder, a missing person, or a nosey photographer. Then Jayne is attacked, and her courage is his undoing. <br /><br />Reed must risk everything to protect her - and find a cunning killer.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11801414234943259293" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1926523241" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1926523241" />
    <a title="&quot;Avonna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5428424-avonna"><img alt="&quot;Avonna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470970273p2/5428424.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1926523241?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="&quot;Avonna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="&quot;Avonna" href="/user/show/5428424-avonna">&quot;Avonna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1926523241" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4013520265102649045">Check out all of my reviews at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.avonnalovesgenres.com'>http://www.avonnalovesgenres.com</a><br/><br/>Rating: 3.5 Stars<br/><br/>I started this suspense series, Midnight Exposure (Midnight, #1) by Melinda Leigh, because I really enjoy her Scarlet Falls series. (Check them out!) <br/><br/>Jayne Sullivan makes her money as a photographer and occasionally for the big money as a tabloid photographer. She is sent to Maine in December to find and photograph the reclusive sculptor R.S. Morgan. She hates being deceitful, but she needs the money to help her bro</span>
  <span id="freeText4013520265102649045" style="display:none">Check out all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.avonnalovesgenres.com">http://www.avonnalovesgenres.com</a><br /><br />Rating: 3.5 Stars<br /><br />I started this suspense series, Midnight Exposure (Midnight, #1) by Melinda Leigh, because I really enjoy her Scarlet Falls series. (Check them out!) <br /><br />Jayne Sullivan makes her money as a photographer and occasionally for the big money as a tabloid photographer. She is sent to Maine in December to find and photograph the reclusive sculptor R.S. Morgan. She hates being deceitful, but she needs the money to help her brothers with the family bar in Philly and medical bills for her youngest brother. She is glad to be away from Philly at the moment also, to get away from a stalker who attacked her and has gone to prison, but he is out and had promised to come for her again.<br /><br />At the address her editor gave her she meets Reed Kimball. Reed had moved to Maine with his son after the death of his wife. He was a homicide detective in his old life, but now acts as a handyman around town and has a secret in his barn turned work shed out behind his home. He hides his true identity from all, but the police chief in town. Jayne does not know the connection between Reed and R.S. Morgan and before she can find out she is abducted. She escapes on her own in a blizzard. Reed finds her and takes her to his home.<br /><br />Both Reed and Jayne are hiding secrets and motives, but they can’t help but continually be attracted to each other. As the sexual tension increases, so does the threat to Jayne from an unknown source which could prove to be deadly.<br /><br />This was a fast paced and exciting read in the first chapter and then again after a few. I just felt it bogged down for a while after the first chapter. I also had a problem with how long it took Reed to tell Jayne about his past. He was reclusive over something that he was proved innocent of doing and after a new scandal comes along, I think the media would have left him and his son alone. He did not even stay in the same town, he moved far away.<br /><br />The Celtic druid facts were interesting and so was the reason for the killings. I do not understand why the other family member was involved though. I do not understand how he could believe a madman. It was a stretch for me. That said, I still like Ms. Leigh’s writing style and will continue on with this series. Not a bad book, but just not my favorite by this author.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4013520265102649045" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12821366881846217279">Halfway through and I have to admit that I'm disappointed in this one. Even it features mature (the h is 30 and the H is old enough to have a 17 year old son), the MCs act like teenagers. The H is afraid to "live again" after his wife's death and the h has a lot of baggage due to an assault. Neither of them want to be attracted to the other and so they push and pull and push and pull. The attraction they feel is pretty superficial, the secrets are being dragged out way longer than normal for thi</span>
  <span id="freeText12821366881846217279" style="display:none">Halfway through and I have to admit that I'm disappointed in this one. Even it features mature (the h is 30 and the H is old enough to have a 17 year old son), the MCs act like teenagers. The H is afraid to "live again" after his wife's death and the h has a lot of baggage due to an assault. Neither of them want to be attracted to the other and so they push and pull and push and pull. The attraction they feel is pretty superficial, the secrets are being dragged out way longer than normal for this author, and I'm having a hard time recognizing this as a Melinda Leigh book.<br /><br />Upon finishing, I'd give this 1.5 stars. The romance rated one star and the mystery was two stars. Unfortunately, this was the first Melinda Leigh book that I found boring and annoying. I'm not sure if I'm going to continue on with this series, but I will definitely continue with Morgan Dane. I adore her and Lance. :)</span>

<div id="review_413267353" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/413267353" />
    <a title="Angela Risner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9972516-angela-risner"><img alt="Angela Risner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338755683p2/9972516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/413267353?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela Risner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela Risner" href="/user/show/9972516-angela-risner">Angela Risner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/15096281-midnight-exposure">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer413267353" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16618851412231189881">I read Melinda Leigh's first book, She Can Run, earlier this year but haven't reviewed it yet. However, I do remember that there were a lot of pluses in her first outing and a few negatives. I thoroughly enjoyed this book and really am pleased to see a lot of growth between that first novel and this one.<br/><br/>This story follows Jayne, who is a photographer trying to make money for her family (three brothers). They all run a bar together in Philadelphia. One of her brothers is suffering from PTSD after</span>
  <span id="freeText16618851412231189881" style="display:none">I read Melinda Leigh's first book, She Can Run, earlier this year but haven't reviewed it yet. However, I do remember that there were a lot of pluses in her first outing and a few negatives. I thoroughly enjoyed this book and really am pleased to see a lot of growth between that first novel and this one.<br /><br />This story follows Jayne, who is a photographer trying to make money for her family (three brothers). They all run a bar together in Philadelphia. One of her brothers is suffering from PTSD after serving in the Middle East and his hospital bills are mounting. Jayne has taken on some tabloid photography assignments because, even though she hates them, they pay the best. She's on the tail of a reclusive sculptor, trying to get pictures for a tabloid magazine. This leads her to a small town in Maine, where former detective Reed Kimball is raising his son. <br /><br />Before Jayne arrived, two high school hikers have disappeared. One body has turned up, but the other hiker is still missing. Jayne becomes wrapped up in the mysterious doings of this small town. Jayne has already suffered an attack from a serial killer and is understandably on edge when someone is clearly stalking her. <br /><br />Of course, there are a lot of foregone conclusions: there will be a romance between the two main characters, Reed will be drawn back into police work to protect Jayne, etc. But the characters come alive and that makes the journey, while predictable in many areas, exciting. I cared about what happened to them, even the supporting cast. <br /><br />I highly recommend this. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16618851412231189881" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_403860245" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/403860245" />
    <a title="Angela Blount" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4269099-angela-blount"><img alt="Angela Blount" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592507072p2/4269099.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/403860245?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela Blount" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela Blount" href="/user/show/4269099-angela-blount">Angela Blount</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/15096281-midnight-exposure">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4269099-angela-blount?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer403860245" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10994802378443425779">Nothing gets the blood pumping like a crazed, homicidal Druid bent on ritual human sacrifice. <br/><br/>Leigh's style is competent and refreshingly plot-heavy, with the romantic elements introduced without force or hurry, despite the one-week time constraint. The hero and heroine are both believable and endearing from early on. And this reviewer particularly appreciated the accurate mentionings of the thrice-killed 'bog bodies' believed to have been a part of ancient Druid rituals intended to ward off an </span>
  <span id="freeText10994802378443425779" style="display:none">Nothing gets the blood pumping like a crazed, homicidal Druid bent on ritual human sacrifice. <br /><br />Leigh's style is competent and refreshingly plot-heavy, with the romantic elements introduced without force or hurry, despite the one-week time constraint. The hero and heroine are both believable and endearing from early on. And this reviewer particularly appreciated the accurate mentionings of the thrice-killed 'bog bodies' believed to have been a part of ancient Druid rituals intended to ward off an impending Roman invasion.<br /><br />Unfortunately, I can't readily recommend this book, as the copy I received was clearly in need of another editorial sweep--aggravatingly riddled with grammatical errors. (Hopefully, it wasn't the final product.) Metaphors are plentiful to the point of distraction, and there were a few too many tidy coincidences driving the plot. <br /><br />The third-person limited viewpoint changes worked well for the first half of the book, primarily alternating between the hero, heroine, and villain. But then as it went on, some readers may find the narrative a bit cluttered as a number of side-character perspectives are added but not repeated. Closure is also a bit lacking, but that could easily be a result of setup--designating this book as the first in an interconnected series.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10994802378443425779" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6807103068856734149">Another exciting thriller from Melinda Leigh. You are shocked within the first 5 pages. Some would fear what is to come after those pages but if you love a good thrilling ride with a side of romance then step on board and hang on. <br/><br/>Jayne Sullivan is a photographer and has come to town looking for the illusive sculptor her sleazy tabloid boss sent her to expose.   <span id="freeText6807103068856734149" style="display:none">Another exciting thriller from Melinda Leigh. You are shocked within the first 5 pages. Some would fear what is to come after those pages but if you love a good thrilling ride with a side of romance then step on board and hang on. <br /><br />Jayne Sullivan is a photographer and has come to town looking for the illusive sculptor her sleazy tabloid boss sent her to expose. She doesn't want to do the job but she needs the money because she feels guilty about not being about to financially help out her brothers. She hasnt had an easy time of it as she was attacked when she was in college and wears the scar from it on her face. <br /><br />Reed Kimball quit his job as a homicide detective and took his son and fled the city 5 years ago when his wife was killed and a media storm converges on them. Reed is also full of scars but his are on the inside. <br /><br />From the outside the little town of Huntsville, Maine looks like a quite peaceful town. What no one realizes is a killer with an agenda is among them. <br /><br />From the first page until the last page our heroine is put through the ringer. There are a few threads not wrapped up at the end of the book. The author has done a great job of hooking this reader for future books in this series. </span>

<div id="review_2346095191" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2346095191" />
    <a title="Emily Crow" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23080450-emily-crow"><img alt="Emily Crow" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1376442423p2/23080450.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2346095191?book_show_action=true">Mar 31, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily Crow" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily Crow" href="/user/show/23080450-emily-crow">Emily Crow</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23080450-emily-crow?shelf=mystery-and-suspense">mystery-and-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23080450-emily-crow?shelf=kindle-unlimited">kindle-unlimited</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23080450-emily-crow?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23080450-emily-crow?shelf=winter-tales">winter-tales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23080450-emily-crow?shelf=romance-challenge-2018">romance-challenge-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23080450-emily-crow?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23080450-emily-crow?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2346095191" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9232708660318151880">*Actual rating 2.5 stars*<br/><br/>I haven't found a romantic suspense novel I've truly enjoyed since the late 1980s, when I binge-read Mary Higgins Clark, and it's hard to say exactly why I can't warm up to this genre. I love romance and I love thrillers and psychological suspense, but for some reason when the two get mixed together, it's usually an awkward reading experience for me. As much as I would love to say that <i>Midnight Exposure</i> is the book that bucked the trend, sadly, that would not be true. Ho</span>
  <span id="freeText9232708660318151880" style="display:none">*Actual rating 2.5 stars*<br /><br />I haven't found a romantic suspense novel I've truly enjoyed since the late 1980s, when I binge-read Mary Higgins Clark, and it's hard to say exactly why I can't warm up to this genre. I love romance and I love thrillers and psychological suspense, but for some reason when the two get mixed together, it's usually an awkward reading experience for me. As much as I would love to say that <i>Midnight Exposure</i> is the book that bucked the trend, sadly, that would not be true. However, I can state that it was mildly entertaining despite some of the cringe-worthy moments it gave me.<br /><br />On the plus side, it is a novel about people being stalked and killed by a homicidal Druid in the Maine woods. Maybe I'm morbid, but that's a fun idea for a thriller. Also, the hero and heroine were both relatively likable...at least likable enough I didn't want them to die. And it was a quick, mindless sort of read, which I am often in the mood for these days.<br /><br />But as to what I didn't like...the simile and metaphor-laden writing and the abundance of cliches. WARNING: mild spoilers to follow. (But I don't give away anything important, like the bad guy's identity. Although if you've read very many suspense novels, you will probably figure that out right away.) <br /><br />To start with, the heroine, Jayne, is working as a tabloid photographer despite her scruples because she has to pay for her little brother's medical bills. (If I had a dollar for every character in a contemporary romance novel who struggles to pay off a relative's medical bills, I'd have enough money to pay for someone else's medical bills, or at least a doctor visit. It's like the easy shorthand to have a character do something weird or problematic for money and still be portrayed as good and noble.) <br /><br />And Jayne has such a tragic history--orphaned at twelve, gave up her carefree youth to cook and clean for her brothers, attacked and almost killed by a stalker in college (so she has to drop out). Then it turns out that the hero, Reed, also has a tragic backstory! Honestly, why can't anyone in this type of novel just be normal? Why always so wounded and tragic?<br /><br />Another cliche--of course, the police are completely incompetent. Prior to Jayne's arrival, two hikers disappeared in the area and then one of them's decapitated body is found. And the police are like, "Well, let's not go crazy folks, we don't know it was murder. This young man could very well have been decapitated by natural causes." <br /><br />But as I said, despite a lot of silliness, it was an okay story. I doubt I will read more by this author, but I'm not wishing I could invent a time machine just to get back the hours of my life it took to read it. <br /><br />Read for Unapologetic Romance Readers 2018 challenge: Romantic Suspense category</span>
  <a data-text-id="9232708660318151880" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_440566268" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/440566268" />
    <a title="Kathleen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4239132-kathleen"><img alt="Kathleen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1312333230p2/4239132.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/440566268?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathleen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathleen" href="/user/show/4239132-kathleen">Kathleen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/15096281-midnight-exposure">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer440566268" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer882572423423704628">Midnight Exposure is a gripping romantic suspense thriller that will keep you sitting on the edge of your seat.<br/><br/>While on a camping/hiking trip in the snowy woods of Maine, college roommates Zack and John for the past two days have become lost in a blinding snowstorm. October 31st ... Halloween ... while searching for signs of civilization they smell smoke and hear faint murmurs of people's voices, they come to a clearing and spot a fire burning and run into a cloaked man with a knife ... unfortun</span>
  <span id="freeText882572423423704628" style="display:none">Midnight Exposure is a gripping romantic suspense thriller that will keep you sitting on the edge of your seat.<br /><br />While on a camping/hiking trip in the snowy woods of Maine, college roommates Zack and John for the past two days have become lost in a blinding snowstorm. October 31st ... Halloween ... while searching for signs of civilization they smell smoke and hear faint murmurs of people's voices, they come to a clearing and spot a fire burning and run into a cloaked man with a knife ... unfortunately they are at the wrong place at the wrong time ... One of the hiker's body has been discovered, but the other hiker is still missing.<br /><br />Two months later on December 15th, photographer Jayne Sullivan, in an attempt to financially help her three brothers save their tavern in Philadelphia, and help pay for brother Danny's Iraq combat related medical bills, has reluctantly taken on an assignment with a one-week deadline for a sleazy tabloid, and traveled to Huntsville, Maine, to track down and photograph the reclusive renowned sculptor, R.S. Morgan.<br /><br />Reed Kimball is an ex-Georgia police detective, who has moved with his seventeen year old son, Scott, to Huntsville, Maine, after the murder of his wife. Seeking seclusion in his forest retreat, this reclusive man is determined to keep his new beginning as a sculptor from being revealed.<br /><br />While searching for the reculsive sculptor, Jayne runs into Reed, who claims to be a handyman. There is an undeniable attraction between them, but secrets from their past, and a serial killer who has targeted Jayne as his next victim, threatens their budding relationship and survival.<br /><br />Midnight Exposure is a riveting fast-paced romantic suspense thriller that will captivate the reader's attention and keep them guessing. Author Melinda Leigh weaves an intriguing tale written in the third person narrative with alternating perspectives from Jayne, Reed and the villain. The story is full of complicated twists and turns that will keep the reader on their toes as the mystery of the characters' and town's secrets unfold. The author's creative writing style tantalizes the reader with clues behind Jayne and Reed's past and secrets coupled with an intriguing look into the mysterious Druid cult's customs and sacrificial rituals. With a great mixture of mystery, suspense and romance, Midnight Exposure is one heck of a page turning thriller that you won't be able to put down.<br /><br />The author creates a cast of characters who are realistic and complex people, with past histories and secrets that draw you into their lives. Jayne and Reed both wear scars from their troubled pasts, there is a palpable emotional pull of strength and feelings that they embrace as survivors. I loved how the author portrayed the villain, he is one creepy dude that is seriously demented, I couldn't help but be intrigued by his obsession with Jayne. With a great supporting cast of characters, a scenic setting rich in detail and vivid description, and a riveting storyline that is so chilling and leaves the reader with an anti-climatic cliffhanger, Midnight Exposure is the first book in a series that will keep you wanting more. The second book in the series, Midnight Sacrifice, will be released in Spring 2013, it will pick up the storyline with the story surrounding around Jayne's brother Danny.<br /><br />Disclaimer: I received a copy of the book from the author in exchange for my honest review, and for hosting a virtual book event on my book review blog site.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://jerseygirlbookreviews.blogspot.com/2012/10/midnight-exposure-by-melinda-leigh.html">http://jerseygirlbookreviews.blogspot...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="882572423423704628" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5709636-anita?shelf=2018-reading-challenge">2018-reading-challenge</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer934474067" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18412693626249110939">This book would have been more interesting without all the romantic angst, which, when the conclusion rolls around, seemed awfully moot, as none of the misunderstandings really affected anyone's feelings.  There was instalust, which quickly became instalove, and a couple who are unwilling to talk to each other, even though they are willing to sleep with each other, and think that they're in love.<br/><br/>At the very least our heroine wasn't TSTL, but that's little consolation for the fact that a whole bu</span>
  <span id="freeText18412693626249110939" style="display:none">This book would have been more interesting without all the romantic angst, which, when the conclusion rolls around, seemed awfully moot, as none of the misunderstandings really affected anyone's feelings.  There was instalust, which quickly became instalove, and a couple who are unwilling to talk to each other, even though they are willing to sleep with each other, and think that they're in love.<br /><br />At the very least our heroine wasn't TSTL, but that's little consolation for the fact that a whole bunch of other stuff in the book bugs the crap out of me.  Not least of all was the way too predictable murder mystery / crime thriller.  I most definitely saw the killer's identity from the beginning.<br /><br />As I have a predisposition to give second chances to an author who didn't thoroughly annoy me--because this book was less frustrating than it was just formulaic and predictable--I will probably move onto the next book and see how that one works out.<br /><br />Otherwise, pending my decision to continue or drop this series, I'll have to move onto my backup series for the <a href="https://anicheungbookabyss.blogspot.com/2018/10/can-you-read-series-in-month-november.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Can You Read a Series in a Month? Challenge</a> for this month.<br /><br />Meanwhile, this book was also read for the <b><a href="https://anicheungbookabyss.blogspot.com/p/the-24-tasks-of-festive-season.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">24 Festive Tasks</a>, Door 18: Winter Solstice / Yuletide:</b><br /><b>'Read any book that takes place in December; OR with ice or snow on the cover; OR that revolves around the (summer or winter) equinox; OR a collection of poetry by Hafez'</b>.<br /><br />This book takes place in December.<br /><br />I'll come back and add the Door's graphic when it is officially revealed!<br /><br /><br /><b>Originally posted at <a href="https://anicheungbookabyss.blogspot.com/2018/11/brief-thoughts-midnight-exposure.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Ani's Book Abyss | Midnight Exposure</a></b></span>

<div id="review_422028920" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/422028920" />
    <a title="Kathy Martin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3122948-kathy-martin"><img alt="Kathy Martin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459738550p2/3122948.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/422028920?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathy Martin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathy Martin" href="/user/show/3122948-kathy-martin">Kathy Martin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/15096281-midnight-exposure">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer422028920" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer427636933381822045">I really enjoyed this romantic suspense title. It had great pacing and was filled with suspense. The tension just kept ramping up and it kept me guessing until almost the very end. <br/><br/>Jayne Sullivan travels to Huntsville, Maine, on the trail of recluse sculptor R. S. Morgan. She is working for a tabloid despite her moral reservations because she needs to make money to help her brother who was injured while serving in Iraq. Jayne is also the survivor of an attack by a man who attacked, raped and kil</span>
  <span id="freeText427636933381822045" style="display:none">I really enjoyed this romantic suspense title. It had great pacing and was filled with suspense. The tension just kept ramping up and it kept me guessing until almost the very end. <br /><br />Jayne Sullivan travels to Huntsville, Maine, on the trail of recluse sculptor R. S. Morgan. She is working for a tabloid despite her moral reservations because she needs to make money to help her brother who was injured while serving in Iraq. Jayne is also the survivor of an attack by a man who attacked, raped and killed two other women. She ended up scarred and with her confidence battered but she is a survivor. She has learned to shoot a gun and do martial arts but she hasn't learned to trust her heart.<br /><br />Jayne didn't expect to meet Reed Kimball who is both sexy and reclusive. He has some major secrets. He has come to Maine to find a quiet life for himself and his seventeen-year-old son. His was a police detective in Georgia when his wife was murdered. He was briefly suspected of her death and became the focus of a media frenzy. He certainly doesn't trust the media now. He is completely determined to keep his second career as a sculptor hidden.<br /><br />While she is looking around the town and taking pictures, she accidentally shoots a picture that brings her to the attention of a local crazy who is planning a Druid ritual that involves human sacrifice. This crazy has already killed a young man who was hiking in the area. His body was found during a warm spell but there was so much damage that the police can't confirm murder. Jayne is kidnapped by this guy but manages to escape and stumble into the path of Reed who was out searching for her. Since they are in the midst of a blizzard, Reed takes her home where their attraction grows. The sexual tension is increasing but both characters' issues keep them apart.<br /><br />Jayne is determined to leave town to get back to the relative safety of her big city life and the care of her brothers. She is also afraid that her stalker might hurt Reed or his son. Reed doesn't want her to go but can't open up enough to ask her to stay. It takes gunfire to force them to acknowledge their attraction.<br /><br />This was a great story. As I was reading it, I was already planning which of my friends to pass this book along to. I know fans of romantic suspense will really enjoy this one. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="427636933381822045" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1926922918" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1926922918" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23102950-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1445470019p2/23102950.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1926922918?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/23102950-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781612184753" href="/book/show/55539333-midnight-exposure">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23102950-melanie?shelf=own-print">own-print</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23102950-melanie?shelf=romantic-suspense">romantic-suspense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1926922918" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1597694587219575377"><i>Midnight Exposure</i> came up recently as a recommendation on my Kindle and despite having never heard of it, I decided to check it out and I'm so glad I did as I ended up really enjoying it!<br/><br/>Jayne Sullivan has taken a photography job with a tabloid to help pay for her brother's medical bills and she's tasked with getting a picture of a reclusive artist in Maine. Kidnapped soon after she arrives, she escapes only to be drawn into an insane game of cat and mouse with a killer obsessed with Celtic cult</span>
  <span id="freeText1597694587219575377" style="display:none"><i>Midnight Exposure</i> came up recently as a recommendation on my Kindle and despite having never heard of it, I decided to check it out and I'm so glad I did as I ended up really enjoying it!<br /><br />Jayne Sullivan has taken a photography job with a tabloid to help pay for her brother's medical bills and she's tasked with getting a picture of a reclusive artist in Maine. Kidnapped soon after she arrives, she escapes only to be drawn into an insane game of cat and mouse with a killer obsessed with Celtic culture and Druid rituals.<br /><br />Right from the start, I really liked Jayne as a character. She's incredibly strong and very capable of looking out for herself. After a past trauma, she took the time to learn to defend herself which helps her out on more than one occasion over the course of <i>Midnight Exposure</i>. I also like that she's able to talk herself down when mentally she reaches her breaking point and doesn't need a man to do that for her. Reed is incredibly supportive of Jayne and thinks its amazing how well she's able to handle herself, but he's also there for her when she does want his support. The romance develops naturally and is very believable for developing over a short period of time. The chemistry between Jayne and Reed certainly helped in that department.<br /><br />The killer being obsessed with Celtic culture and Druid rituals made the suspense part of the plot really interesting. The killer's motives were fascinating and not what I was expecting. I had a few guesses of who the killer may be and one of those guesses ended up being correct. Being right on who the killer was didn't detract from my enjoyment of the book at all though. I still very much enjoyed finding out the whys and for the 'final showdown' romantic suspense books always have.<br /><br />Overall, <i>Midnight Exposure</i> was a very enjoyable read and I definitely recommend it to fans of the romantic suspense genre or anyone looking for a quick read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1597694587219575377" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_393377914" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/393377914" />
    <a title="Laurel-Rain" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1402123-laurel-rain"><img alt="Laurel-Rain" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591104726p2/1402123.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/393377914?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laurel-Rain" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laurel-Rain" href="/user/show/1402123-laurel-rain">Laurel-Rain</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/15096281-midnight-exposure">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer393377914" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12235466106637056588">When Jayne Sullivan headed to a small town in Maine, she was determined to capture images of a reclusive artist. But almost from the very first moments after her arrival, nothing is turning out to be what she expected.<br/><br/>First she is captivated by a mysterious handyman, Reed Kimball, and then she begins to discover various townspeople who seem to vary from unfriendly to strange.<br/><br/>While sorting out the events as they unfold, and before she can catch her breath, she is abducted and held prisoner in a d</span>
  <span id="freeText12235466106637056588" style="display:none">When Jayne Sullivan headed to a small town in Maine, she was determined to capture images of a reclusive artist. But almost from the very first moments after her arrival, nothing is turning out to be what she expected.<br /><br />First she is captivated by a mysterious handyman, Reed Kimball, and then she begins to discover various townspeople who seem to vary from unfriendly to strange.<br /><br />While sorting out the events as they unfold, and before she can catch her breath, she is abducted and held prisoner in a damp basement, with no hope that she'll ever escape. Her captor wears a mask and a cloak, and all she can see is a pair of intense blue eyes.<br /><br />Fortunately, she is trained in martial arts and is able to break free, using skill and the element of surprise. But her journey toward finding the answers to the strange goings-on in this frightening town are only beginning. And never mind ever finding the artist who is definitely determined to hide.<br /><br />Who can she trust and what can she know to be true? Suddenly everyone starts to look like the potential abductor and any pair of blue eyes could be those of her captor. Can she even believe in the goodness in Reed, who rescued her on the road after her escape?<br /><br />All of the characters in "Midnight Exposure" seemed potentially suspect, including law enforcement. Even as I started to figure out who might have targeted Jayne and several others, I was thrown a curve at the end of this exciting page-turner that was a great mix of mystery and romance. As much as I enjoyed this book, I had trouble liking most of the characters. The author's ability to evoke emotions with her characterizations is a plus. The motivations that drove the killer stretched credibility, however, so I'm awarding this one four stars. Recommended for fans of suspense and romance. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12235466106637056588" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2017807680" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2017807680" />
    <a title="Taqiyyah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9867032-taqiyyah"><img alt="Taqiyyah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338324783p2/9867032.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2017807680?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Taqiyyah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Taqiyyah" href="/user/show/9867032-taqiyyah">Taqiyyah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/20500215-midnight-exposure">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2017807680" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12654954242454458998"><strong>Cliche </strong><br/><br/>It's an okay book but I could tell from the get go who the culprit will be. The only reason I finished it was because I had to be in lab and babysit my experiment.. that being said I have now read three of her books and they all follow a pattern. Furthermore, I believe the writing is repetitive, five different senescence with same words replaced by synonyms. It's filled with romance and emotions stereotypically associated with women. Even though the female characters are supposed to be ca</span>
  <span id="freeText12654954242454458998" style="display:none"><strong>Cliche </strong><br /><br />It's an okay book but I could tell from the get go who the culprit will be. The only reason I finished it was because I had to be in lab and babysit my experiment.. that being said I have now read three of her books and they all follow a pattern. Furthermore, I believe the writing is repetitive, five different senescence with same words replaced by synonyms. It's filled with romance and emotions stereotypically associated with women. Even though the female characters are supposed to be career women, their mushy words and behaviour contradict that. <br /><br />I find following things really annoying and if you don't feel free to spend your time reading. <br />1- unnecessary romance at totally inappropriate times for e.g. there is a serial killer after the girl and all she cares about is a man's strong chest or feeling "protected" in his muscles arms. As a woman and a human being myself it's very hard to digest.<br /><br />2- beauty/physical appeal of characters is exaggerated. It's in every one of the books I read. In real life I am yet to meet/see a single person who just blows me away with a single glance. Come on.<br /><br />3-The whole damaged people routine is super cliche. Can't one normal person without a harrowing past be the main character for once. Either the main character's wife/husband died or their folks have mental illness or they survived an attack and the list goes on and all these unfortunate people end up being attracted to each other. <br /><br />4- There are extreme emotions of love and sadness. Too many "cute" moments.. the copulation scenes especially go on and on.. if I need that I will read Danielle Steele not a thriller.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12654954242454458998" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2614168713" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2614168713" />
    <a title="Renee " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6593014-renee"><img alt="Renee " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1429122769p2/6593014.jpg" /></a>

It wasn't bad, but it was nothing to write home about either. This was my first Melinda Leigh book. <br/><br/>I've always struggled with the insta "love" thing in stories. I've also struggled with the amount of traumatic ways one of the characters can be placed in and experience but then walk away as if it never happened. It's almost like there's someth</span>
  <span id="freeText13252818114446319202" style="display:none">2018 Reading Challenge: A book with a time of day in the title<br /><br />The 2 stars stands for "it was ok" and that really about sums up how I feel about this book. It wasn't bad, but it was nothing to write home about either. This was my first Melinda Leigh book. <br /><br />I've always struggled with the insta "love" thing in stories. I've also struggled with the amount of traumatic ways one of the characters can be placed in and experience but then walk away as if it never happened. It's almost like there's something missing in the middle. <br /><br />Reed Kimbrall<br />Jayne Sullivan<br /><br />Rating: R -blood and guts, shootings, witchcraft<br />Language: -profanity including use of deity<br />Recommend: -yes</span>

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('0hrgY94rYMU2Ffeht2BcUGDtCDBN4dDWpaaKvnib01jrIC1EOPEeR36UadedGRO+9WYZEyQmMolrEk94i7sbWA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xfZVdrMnPEE1WmTBOo3WyzI6/pLj7UeZR9u8IEkdBcb8zJhRVf1Cw33b+rcQ9Jklp7HvsYoqpcaJb3nmuj3Nxg==')})
  }
//]]>

<span id="freeTextContainer17706137206501725587">#1 Wall Street Journal and #1 Amazon bestselling author Melinda Leigh is a fully recovered banker who learned that writing books is way more fun than analyzing financial statements. Melinda’s debut novel, SHE CAN RUN, was nominated for Best First Novel by the International Thriller Writers. Since then, she has garnered numerous writing accolades, including two RITA® Award nominations and an induct</span>
  <span id="freeText17706137206501725587" style="display:none">#1 Wall Street Journal and #1 Amazon bestselling author Melinda Leigh is a fully recovered banker who learned that writing books is way more fun than analyzing financial statements. Melinda’s debut novel, SHE CAN RUN, was nominated for Best First Novel by the International Thriller Writers. Since then, she has garnered numerous writing accolades, including two RITA® Award nominations and an induction into the NJ Romance Writers Hall of Fame. Her novels have sold more than 7.5 million copies across the world. Melinda loves martial arts, rescue dogs, and sea turtles. <br /><br /><b>WEBSITE: </b><a href="https://www.melindaeigh.com" rel="nofollow noopener">https://www.melindaleigh.com/</a><br /><br /><b>FACEBOOK: </b><a href="https://www.facebook.com/melindaleighauthorpage/" rel="nofollow noopener">https://www.facebook.com/melindaleighauthorpage/</a><br /><br /><b>TWITTER: </b><a href="https://twitter.com/MelindaLeigh1" rel="nofollow noopener">https://twitter.com/MelindaLeigh1</a></span>
